<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">




<DIV align="center" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 18pt"><B>SANDISK CORPORATION</B>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left">
<A name="106"></A>
</DIV>
<DIV align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>NOTES TO CONDENSED CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS</B></DIV>


<DIV align="center" style="font-size: 10pt"><B>(Unaudited)</B></DIV>



<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>1. Organization and Summary of Significant Accounting Policies</B>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;These interim condensed consolidated financial statements are unaudited but reflect, in the
opinion of management, all adjustments, consisting of normal recurring adjustments and accruals,
necessary to present fairly the financial position of SanDisk Corporation and its subsidiaries (the
&#147;Company&#148;) as of April&nbsp;2, 2006, and the statements of income and cash flows for the three months
ended April&nbsp;2, 2006 and April&nbsp;3, 2005. Certain information and footnote disclosures normally
included in financial statements prepared in accordance with U.S. generally accepted accounting
principles, or GAAP, have been omitted in accordance with the rules and regulations of the
Securities and Exchange Commission, or SEC. These condensed consolidated financial statements
should be read in conjunction with the audited consolidated financial statements and accompanying
notes included in the Company&#146;s most recent annual report on Form 10-K. Certain prior period
amounts have been reclassified to conform to the current period presentation. The results of
operations for the first three months of fiscal 2006 are not necessarily indicative of the results
to be expected for the entire fiscal year.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company&#146;s fiscal year ends on the Sunday closest to December&nbsp;31, and its fiscal quarters
end on the Sunday closest to March&nbsp;31, June&nbsp;30, and September&nbsp;30. The first quarters of fiscal
2006 and fiscal 2005 ended on April&nbsp;2, 2006 and April&nbsp;3, 2005, respectively. Fiscal year 2006 ends
on December&nbsp;31, 2006 and fiscal year 2005 ended on January&nbsp;1, 2006.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Organization and Nature of Operations. </I>SanDisk Corporation (together with its subsidiaries,
the Company) was incorporated in Delaware on June&nbsp;1, 1988. The Company designs, develops and
markets flash storage card products used in a wide variety of consumer electronics products. The
Company operates in one segment, flash memory storage products.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Principles of Consolidation. </I>The consolidated financial statements include the accounts of
the Company and its majority-owned subsidiaries. All intercompany balances and transactions have
been eliminated.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Use of Estimates. </I>The preparation of financial statements in conformity with GAAP requires
management to make estimates and assumptions that affect the amounts reported in the financial
statements and accompanying notes. The estimates and judgments affect the reported amounts of
assets, liabilities, revenues and expenses, and related disclosure of contingent liabilities. On
an on-going basis, the Company evaluates its estimates, including those related to customer
programs and incentives, product returns, bad debts, inventories and related reserves, investments,
income taxes, warranty obligations, restructuring and contingencies, stock compensation and
litigation. The Company bases estimates on historical experience and on other assumptions that its
management believes are reasonable under the circumstances. These estimates form the basis for
making judgments about the carrying values of assets and liabilities when those values are not
readily apparent from other sources. Actual results could differ from these estimates.
</DIV>

<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">6
</DIV>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always"><A HREF="#tocpage">Table of Contents</A></H5><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">

<DIV align="center" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 18pt"><B>NOTES TO CONDENSED CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS (Cont&#146;d)</B>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>2. Stock-Based Compensation</B>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><B><I>Stock-Based Benefit Plans</I></B>

</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>2005 Stock Incentive Plan</I>. In May&nbsp;2005, the Company&#146;s board of directors adopted the 2005
Employee Incentive Plan (the &#147;2005 Plan&#148;). The shares may be issued under the 2005 Plan pursuant
to three separate equity incentive programs: (i)&nbsp;the discretionary grant program under which stock
options and stock appreciation rights may be granted to officers and other employees, non-employee
board members and independent consultants, (ii)&nbsp;the stock issuance program under which shares may
be awarded to such individuals through restricted stock or restricted stock unit awards or as a
stock bonus for services rendered the Company and (iii)&nbsp;an automatic grant program for the
non-employee board members pursuant to which such individuals will receive option grants or other
stock awards at designated intervals over their period of board service. Grants and awards under
this discretionary grant and stock issuance programs will generally vest as follows: 25% of the
shares will vest on the first anniversary of the vesting commencement date and the remaining 75%
will vest proportionately each quarter over the next 36&nbsp;months of continued service, and the grants
under the automatic grant program will vest in accordance with the specific vesting provisions set
forth in that program. A total of 5,700,000 shares of the Company&#146;s common stock have been
reserved for issuance under this plan. The share reserve may increase by up to an additional
10,000,000 shares to the extent that outstanding options under the 1995 Stock Option Plan and the
1995 Non-Employee Directors Stock Option Plan expire or terminate unexercised. All options granted
under the 2005 Plan were granted with an exercise price equal to the fair market value of the
common stock and will expire seven years from the date of grant. Through April&nbsp;2, 2006, options to
purchase a total of 5,716,836 common shares were granted to employees under the 2005 Plan, net of
cancellations. For the three months ended April&nbsp;2, 2006, options to purchase a total of 4,053,023
common shares were granted to employees under the 2005 Plan, net of cancellations.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>1995 Stock Option Plan and 1995 Non-Employee Directors Stock Option Plan. </I>Both of these plans
terminated on May&nbsp;27, 2005, and no further option grants were made under the plans after that date.
However, options which were outstanding under these plans on May&nbsp;27, 2005 will continue to be
governed by their existing terms and may be exercised for shares of the Company&#146;s common stock at
any time prior to the expiration of the ten-year option term or any earlier termination of those
options in connection with the optionee&#146;s cessation of employment or service with the Company.
Grants and awards under this discretionary grant and stock issuance programs will generally vest as
follows: 25% of the shares will vest on the first anniversary of the vesting commencement date and
the remaining 75% will vest proportionately each quarter over the next 36&nbsp;months of continued
service. As of April&nbsp;2, 2006, options granted, net of cancellations, was 38,568,969 shares and
1,616,000 shares under the 1995 Stock Option Plan and the 1995 Non-Employee Directors Stock Option
Plan, respectively.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>2005 Employee Stock Purchase Plan. </I>The 2005 Employee Stock Purchase Plan (&#147;ESPP&#148;) was
approved by the stockholders on May&nbsp;27, 2005. The ESPP plan consist of two components: a component
for employees residing in the United States and an international component for employees who are
non-U.S. residents. The ESPP plan allows eligible employees to purchase shares of the Company&#146;s
common stock at the end of each six-month offering period at a purchase price equal to 85% of the
lower of the fair market value per share on the start date of the offering period or the fair
market value per share on the purchase date. As of April&nbsp;2, 2006, a total of 5,000,000 shares were
reserved for issuance and 113,909 shares had been issued under the ESPP plan.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B><I>Adoption of SFAS 123(R)</I></B>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Effective January&nbsp;2, 2006, the Company adopted the fair value recognition provisions of
Statement of Financial Accounting Standards No.&nbsp;123(R), SFAS 123(R), <I>Share-Based Payment</I>, using the
modified-prospective transition method and therefore have not restated its financial results for
prior periods. Under that transition method, for awards expected to vest, compensation cost
recognized in the three months ended April&nbsp;2, 2006 includes the following: (a)&nbsp;compensation cost,
based on the grant-date estimated fair value and expense attribution method elected upon the
Company&#146;s adoption of SFAS 123, related to any share-based awards granted through, but not yet
vested as of January&nbsp;1, 2006, and (b)&nbsp;compensation cost for any share-based awards granted on or
subsequent to January&nbsp;2, 2006, based on the grant-date fair value estimated in accordance with the
provisions of SFAS 123(R). The Company recognized compensation expense for the fair values of
these awards, which have graded vesting, on a straight-line basis over the requisite service period
of each of these awards, net of estimated forfeitures.
</DIV>

<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">7
</DIV>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always"><A HREF="#tocpage">Table of Contents</A></H5><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">

<DIV align="center" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 18pt"><B>NOTES TO CONDENSED CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS (Cont&#146;d)</B>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company estimates the fair value of stock options granted using the Black-Scholes-Merton
option-pricing formula and a single option award approach. The Company&#146;s expected term represents
the period that the Company&#146;s stock-based awards are expected to be outstanding and was determined
based on historical experience of similar awards, giving consideration to the
contractual terms of the stock-based awards. The Company&#146;s expected volatility is based on
the implied volatility of its traded options and the Company considered the guidance provided by
the U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission&#146;s Staff Accounting Bulletin 107 to place exclusive
reliance on implied volatilities to estimate our stock volatility over the expected term of our
awards. The Company has historically not paid dividends and has no foreseeable plans to issue
dividends. The risk-free interest rate is based on the yield from U.S. Treasury zero-coupon bonds
with an equivalent term.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;As a result of adopting SFAS 123(R), the impact to the Condensed Consolidated Financial
Statements for the three months ended April&nbsp;2, 2006 for income before income taxes and net income
for the three months ended April&nbsp;2, 2006 was $18.8&nbsp;million and $12.9&nbsp;million lower, respectively,
than if we had continued to account for stock-based compensation under APB 25. The impact on both
basic and diluted earnings per share for the three months ended April&nbsp;2, 2006 was $0.07 and $0.06
per share, respectively. In addition, prior to the adoption of
SFAS&nbsp;<Font Style="White-space:nowrap">123(R)</FONT>, the Company presented
the tax benefit of stock option exercises as operating cash flows.
Upon the adoption of SFAS&nbsp;123(R), tax benefits resulting from tax deductions in excess of the compensation cost recognized
for those options are classified as financing cash flows.
</DIV>

<DIV align="center" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 18pt"><B>NOTES TO CONDENSED CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS (Cont&#146;d)</B>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B><I>Restricted Stock</I></B>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Restricted stock and restricted stock units are converted into shares of the Company&#146;s common
stock upon vesting on a one-for-one basis. Typically, vesting of restricted stock is subject to
the employee&#146;s continuing service to the Company. The cost of these awards is determined using the
fair value of the Company&#146;s common stock on the date of the grant, and compensation is recognized
over the requisite service period. Restricted stock generally vest over four years.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;A summary of the changes in restricted stock units outstanding under the Company&#146;s equity

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In accordance with Statement of Financial Accounting Standards No.&nbsp;142, or SFAS 142, <I>Goodwill
and Other Intangible Assets</I>, goodwill is not amortized, but instead is reviewed and tested for
impairment at least annually and whenever events or circumstances occur which indicate that
goodwill might be impaired. Impairment of goodwill is tested at the Company&#146;s reporting unit level
by comparing the carrying amount, including goodwill, to the fair value. In performing the
analysis, the Company uses the best information available, including reasonable and supportable
assumptions and projections. If the carrying amount of the reporting unit exceeds its implied fair
value, goodwill is considered impaired and a second step is performed to measure the amount of
impairment loss, if any. The Company will perform an annual review of goodwill with an effective
date of the first day of the fourth fiscal quarter of every fiscal year.
</DIV>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always"><A HREF="#tocpage">Table of Contents</A></H5><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">

<DIV align="center" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 18pt"><B>NOTES TO CONDENSED CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS (Cont&#146;d)</B>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>8. Commitments, Contingencies and Guarantees</B>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt"><B><I>Commitments</I></B>

</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>FlashVision. </I>The Company has a 49.9% ownership interest in FlashVision, a business venture
with Toshiba Corporation, or Toshiba, formed in fiscal 2000. The Company and Toshiba have
collaborated in the development and manufacture of NAND flash memory products. These NAND flash
memory products are manufactured by Toshiba at its 200-millimeter wafer fabrication facilities,
located in Yokkaichi, Japan, using the semiconductor manufacturing equipment owned or leased by
FlashVision. FlashVision purchases wafers from Toshiba at cost and then resells those wafers to
the Company and Toshiba at cost plus a mark-up. Toshiba owns 50.1% of this venture. The Company
accounts for its 49.9% ownership position in FlashVision under the equity method of accounting.
The terms of the FlashVision venture contractually obligate the Company to purchase half of
FlashVision&#146;s NAND wafer supply. The Company can not estimate the total amount of this commitment
as of April&nbsp;2, 2006, because it is based upon future costs and volumes. In addition, the Company
is committed to fund 49.9% of FlashVision&#146;s costs to the extent that FlashVision&#146;s revenues from
wafer sales to the Company and Toshiba are insufficient to cover these costs.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;As of April&nbsp;2, 2006, the Company had notes receivable from FlashVision of 7.3&nbsp;billion Japanese
yen, or approximately $62&nbsp;million based upon the exchange rate at April&nbsp;2, 2006. These notes are
secured by the equipment purchased by FlashVision using the note proceeds.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Flash Partners</I>. The Company has a 49.9% ownership interest in Flash Partners, a business
venture with Toshiba, formed in fiscal 2004. The Company and Toshiba have collaborated in the
development and manufacture of NAND flash memory products. These NAND flash memory products are
manufactured by Toshiba at the 300-millimeter wafer fabrication facility, Fab 3, located in
Yokkaichi, Japan, using the semiconductor manufacturing equipment owned or leased by Flash
Partners. Flash Partners purchases wafers from Toshiba at cost and then resells those wafers to
the Company and Toshiba at cost plus a mark-up. Toshiba owns 50.1% of this venture. The Company
accounts for its 49.9% ownership position in Flash Partners under the equity method of accounting.
The Company is committed to purchase half of Flash Partners&#146; NAND wafer supply. The Company can
not estimate the total amount of this commitment as of April&nbsp;2, 2006, because it is based upon
future costs and volumes. In addition, the Company is committed to fund 49.9% of Flash Partners&#146;
costs to the extent that Flash Partners&#146; revenues from wafer sales to the Company and Toshiba are
insufficient to cover these costs.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;As of April&nbsp;2, 2006, the Company and Toshiba committed to expand Flash Partners&#146; capacity to
70,000 wafer starts per month. The Company currently estimates the total equipment funding
obligation at the 70,000 wafer starts per month level to be approximately 363.1&nbsp;billion Japanese
yen, or approximately $3.1&nbsp;billion based upon the exchange rate at April&nbsp;2, 2006. Of this amount,
the Company is obligated to fund 181.5&nbsp;billion Japanese yen, or approximately $1.5&nbsp;billion based
upon the exchange rate at April&nbsp;2, 2006, of which approximately $0.8&nbsp;billion was left to fund as of
April&nbsp;2, 2006. After considering the commitments between the Company and Toshiba to expand
capacity at Flash Partners, the Company continues to not be the primary beneficiary of Flash
Partners. Subsequent to April&nbsp;2, 2006, the Company amended the funding obligation. See
Note 14, &#147;Subsequent Events.&#148;
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;As of April&nbsp;2, 2006, Flash Partners had utilized operating lease facilities of 85.0&nbsp;billion
Japanese yen, or approximately $724&nbsp;million based on the exchange rate at April&nbsp;2, 2006. As of
April&nbsp;2, 2006, the Company&#146;s guarantee of the Flash Partners&#146; operating lease obligation, net of
accumulated lease payments, was approximately 40.3&nbsp;billion Japanese yen, or approximately $343
million based upon the exchange rate at April&nbsp;2, 2006. In addition, Flash Partners expects to
secure additional equipment lease facilities over time, which the Company may be obligated to
guarantee in whole or in part. See &#147;Off Balance Sheet Liabilities&#148; below.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;As a part of the FlashVision and Flash Partners venture agreements, the Company is required to
fund direct and common research and development expenses related to the development of advanced
NAND flash memory technologies. In fiscal 2004, the Company and Toshiba increased the maximum
quarterly amounts the Company may be required to pay under these agreements and clarified the
allocation methodologies for direct research and development costs. As of April&nbsp;2, 2006, the
Company had accrued liabilities related to these expenses of $6.0&nbsp;million.
</DIV>

<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">14
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Toshiba Foundry. </I>The Company has the ability to purchase additional capacity under a foundry
arrangement with Toshiba. Under the terms of this agreement, the Company is required to provide
Toshiba with a purchase order commitment based on a six-month rolling forecast.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Business Ventures and Foundry Arrangement with Toshiba. </I>Purchase orders placed under the
Toshiba ventures and foundry arrangement with Toshiba relating to the first three months of the
six-month forecast are binding and cannot be canceled. At April&nbsp;2, 2006, the Company had
approximately $121.1&nbsp;million of noncancelable purchase orders for flash memory wafers outstanding
to FlashVision, Flash Partners and Toshiba.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Other Silicon Sources. </I>The Company&#146;s contracts with its other sources of silicon wafers
generally require the Company to provide purchase order commitments based on six-month rolling
forecasts. The purchase orders placed under these arrangements relating to the first three months
of the six-month forecast are generally binding and cannot be canceled. Outstanding purchase
commitments for other sources of silicon wafers are included as part of the total &#147;Noncancelable
production purchase commitments&#148; in the &#147;Contractual Obligations&#148; table below.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Subcontractors. </I>In the normal course of business, the Company&#146;s subcontractors periodically
procure production materials based on the forecast the Company provides to them. The Company&#146;s
agreements with these subcontractors require that it reimburse them for materials that are
purchased on the Company&#146;s behalf in accordance with such forecast. Accordingly, the Company may
be committed to certain costs over and above its open noncancelable purchase orders with these
subcontractors. Outstanding purchase commitments for subcontractors are included as part of the
total &#147;Noncancelable production purchase commitments&#148; in the &#147;Contractual Obligations&#148; table below.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B><I>Off Balance Sheet Liabilities</I></B>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>FlashVision. </I>In May&nbsp;2002, FlashVision secured an equipment lease arrangement of approximately
37.9&nbsp;billion Japanese yen, or approximately $322&nbsp;million based upon the exchange rate at April&nbsp;2,
2006, with Mizuho Leasing, and other financial institutions. Under the terms of the lease, Toshiba
guaranteed these commitments on behalf of FlashVision. The Company agreed to indemnify Toshiba for
certain liabilities Toshiba incurs as a result of Toshiba&#146;s guarantee of the FlashVision equipment
lease arrangement. If FlashVision fails to meet its lease commitments, and Toshiba fulfills these
commitments under the terms of Toshiba&#146;s guarantee, then the Company will be obligated to reimburse
Toshiba for 49.9% of any claims and associated expenses under the lease, unless the claims result
from Toshiba&#146;s failure to meet its obligations to FlashVision or its covenants to the lenders.
Because FlashVision&#146;s equipment lease arrangement is denominated in Japanese yen, the maximum
amount of the Company&#146;s contingent indemnification obligation on a given date when converted to
U.S. dollars will fluctuate based on the exchange rate in effect on that date. As of April&nbsp;2,
2006, the maximum amount of the Company&#146;s contingent indemnification obligation, which reflects
payments and any lease adjustments, was approximately 8.2&nbsp;billion Japanese yen, or approximately
$70&nbsp;million based upon the exchange rate at April&nbsp;2, 2006.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Flash Partners. </I>As described in &#147;Commitments &#151; Flash Partners&#148; above, Flash Partners intends
to sell and lease-back from a consortium of financial institutions a portion of its tools and has
entered into two equipment lease agreements as described below.
</DIV>

<DIV style="margin-top: 6pt">
<TABLE width="100%" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="font-size: 10pt">

<TR valign="top" style="font-size: 10pt; color: #000000; background: transparent">
    <TD width="6%" style="background: transparent">&nbsp;</TD>
    <TD width="3%" nowrap align="left"><B>&#149;</B></TD>
    <TD width="1%">&nbsp;</TD>
    <TD>In December&nbsp;2004, Flash Partners entered into a master lease agreement with certain
financial institutions providing for up to 50.0&nbsp;billion Japanese yen, or approximately
$426&nbsp;million based upon the exchange rate at April&nbsp;2, 2006, of original lease
obligations. As of April&nbsp;2, 2006, Flash Partners had drawn down this entire master
lease facility. The Company and Toshiba have each guaranteed, on a several basis, 50%
of Flash Partners&#146; obligations under the master lease agreement. Lease payments are due
quarterly and will be completed in stages through 2010. At the end of the lease term,
Flash Partners has the option of purchasing the tools from the lessors. Flash Partners
is obligated to insure the equipment, maintain the equipment in accordance with the
manufacturers&#146; recommendations and comply with other customary terms to protect the
leased assets. The master lease agreement contains customary events of default for a
Japanese lease facility and is an exhibit to the Company&#146;s most recent annual report on
Form 10-K. That agreement should be read carefully in its entirety for a comprehensive
understanding of its terms and the nature of the obligations the Company guaranteed.</TD>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B><I>Guarantees</I></B>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Indemnification Agreements. </I>The Company has agreed to indemnify suppliers and customers for
alleged patent infringement. The scope of such indemnity varies, but may, in some instances,
include indemnification for damages and expenses, including attorneys&#146; fees. The Company may
periodically engage in litigation as a result of these indemnification obligations. The Company&#146;s
insurance policies exclude coverage for third-party claims for patent infringement. Although the
liability is not remote, the nature of the patent infringement indemnification obligations prevents
the Company from making a reasonable estimate of the maximum potential amount it could be required
to pay to its suppliers and customers. Historically, the Company has not made any significant
indemnification payments under any such agreements. As of April&nbsp;2, 2006, no amount has been
accrued in the accompanying condensed consolidated financial statements with respect to these
indemnification guarantees.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;As permitted under Delaware law and the Company&#146;s charter and bylaws, the Company has
agreements whereby it indemnifies certain of its officers and each of its directors for certain
events or occurrences while the officer or director is, or was, serving at the Company&#146;s request in
such capacity. The term of the indemnification period is for the officer&#146;s or director&#146;s lifetime.
The maximum potential amount of future payments the Company could be required to make under these
indemnification agreements is unlimited; however, the Company has a Director and Officer insurance
policy that may reduce its exposure and enable it to recover all or a portion of any future amounts
paid. As a result of its insurance policy coverage, the Company believes the estimated fair value
of these indemnification agreements is minimal. The Company has no liabilities recorded for these
agreements as of April&nbsp;2, 2006 or January&nbsp;1, 2006, as this liability is not reasonably estimable
even though liability under these agreements is not remote.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company and Toshiba have agreed to mutually contribute to, and indemnify each other and
Flash Partners for, environmental remediation costs or liability resulting from Flash Partners&#146;
manufacturing operations in certain circumstances. In 2004, the Company and Toshiba each engaged
consultants to perform a review of the existing environmental conditions at the site of the
facility in which Flash Partners operations are located to establish a baseline for evaluating
future environmental conditions. The Company and Toshiba have also entered into a Patent
Indemnification Agreement under which in many cases the Company will share in the expenses
associated with the defense and cost of settlement associated with such claims. This agreement
provides limited protection for the Company against third-party claims that NAND flash memory
products manufactured and sold by Flash Partners infringe third-party patents. The Company has not
made any indemnification payments under any such agreements and as of April&nbsp;2, 2006, no amounts
have been accrued in the accompanying condensed consolidated financial statements with respect to
these indemnification guarantees.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;See also &#147;Off Balance Sheet Liabilities.&#148;
</DIV>

<DIV align="center" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 18pt"><B>NOTES TO CONDENSED CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS (Cont&#146;d)</B>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B><I>Foreign Currency Exchange Contracts</I></B>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company&#146;s objective for holding derivatives is to minimize the material risks associated
with non-functional currency transactions. The Company does not enter into derivatives for
speculative or trading purposes. The Company&#146;s derivative instruments are recorded at fair value
on the balance sheet with changes in fair value recorded in other income (expense). The Company
had foreign currency exchange contract lines available in the amount of $1.24&nbsp;billion at April&nbsp;2,
2006 to enter into foreign currency forward contracts. As of April&nbsp;2, 2006, the Company had
foreign currency forward contracts in place with a notional amount of 4.4&nbsp;billion Japanese yen, or
approximately $37&nbsp;million based upon the exchange rate at April&nbsp;2, 2006. The fair value of these
foreign currency forward contracts as of April&nbsp;2, 2006 was immaterial. The realized gains and
losses on foreign currency forward contracts for the three months ended April&nbsp;2, 2006 were
immaterial.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>9. Business Ventures and Strategic Investments</B>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Tower Semiconductor. </I>The Company owns approximately 14% of the outstanding shares of Tower
Semiconductor Ltd., or Tower, one of its suppliers of wafers for its controller components. The
Company has sourced controller wafers from Tower since the third quarter of fiscal 2003. As of
April&nbsp;2, 2006, the Company owned approximately 10.4&nbsp;million Tower shares with a carrying value and
market value of $12.9&nbsp;million and $13.4&nbsp;million, respectively, a warrant to purchase 0.4&nbsp;million
Tower ordinary shares at an exercise price of $7.50 per share, with a carrying value of zero and
Tower prepaid wafer credits with a carrying value of zero. In addition, the Company holds a Tower
convertible debenture with a carrying value and market value of $4.1&nbsp;million.
</DIV>

<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">18
</DIV>

<!-- PAGEBREAK -->
<P><HR noshade><P>
<H5 align="left" style="page-break-before:always"><A HREF="#tocpage">Table of Contents</A></H5><P>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">

<DIV align="center" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 18pt"><B>NOTES TO CONDENSED CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS (Cont&#146;d)</B>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>10. Related Parties</B>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Toshiba. </I>The Company and Toshiba have collaborated in the development and manufacture of NAND
flash memory products. These NAND flash memory products are manufactured by Toshiba at Toshiba&#146;s
Yokkaichi, Japan operations using the semiconductor manufacturing equipment owned or leased by
FlashVision or Flash Partners. See also Note 8, &#147;Commitments, Contingencies and Guarantees.&#148; The
Company purchased NAND flash memory wafers from FlashVision, Flash Partners and Toshiba totaling
approximately $174.6&nbsp;million and $114.3&nbsp;million in the three months ended April&nbsp;2, 2006 and April
3, 2005, respectively. The purchases of NAND flash memory wafers are ultimately reflected as a
component of the Company&#146;s cost of product revenues. At April&nbsp;2, 2006 and January&nbsp;1, 2006, the
Company had accounts payable balances due to FlashVision of $18.3&nbsp;million and $23.0&nbsp;million,
respectively, balances due to Flash Partners of $32.4&nbsp;million and $27.0&nbsp;million, respectively, and
balances due to Toshiba of $15.2&nbsp;million and $11.7&nbsp;million, respectively. At April&nbsp;2, 2006 and
January&nbsp;1, 2006, the Company had accrued current liabilities due to Toshiba for shared research and
development expenses of $6.0&nbsp;million and $4.2&nbsp;million, respectively.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Tower. </I>The Company owns approximately 14% of the outstanding shares of Tower, has prepaid
wafer credits issued by Tower, and has convertible debt and a warrant to purchase Tower ordinary
shares. The Company&#146;s Chief Executive Officer is a member of the Tower board of directors. The
Company purchased approximately $6.6&nbsp;million and $10.1&nbsp;million in the three months ended April&nbsp;2,
2006 and April&nbsp;3, 2005, respectively, of controller wafers and related non-recurring engineering,
or NRE. These purchases of controller wafers are ultimately reflected as a component of the
Company&#146;s cost of product revenues. At April&nbsp;2, 2006 and January&nbsp;1, 2006, the Company had amounts
payable to Tower of approximately $2.5&nbsp;million and $2.4&nbsp;million, respectively, related to the
purchase of controller wafers and related NRE. See Note 9, &#147;Business Ventures and Strategic
Investments &#151; Tower Semiconductor.&#148;
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Flextronics. </I>The Chairman of Flextronics International, Ltd., or Flextronics, has served on
the Company&#146;s Board of Directors since September&nbsp;2003. For the three months ended April&nbsp;2, 2006
and April&nbsp;3, 2005, the Company recorded revenues related to Flextronics and its affiliates of $19.2
million and $3.8&nbsp;million, respectively, and at April&nbsp;2, 2006 and January&nbsp;1, 2006, the Company had
receivables from Flextronics and its affiliates of $16.3&nbsp;million and $12.5&nbsp;million, respectively.
In addition, the Company purchased from Flextronics and its affiliates $14.4&nbsp;million and $10.6
million of services for card assembly and testing in the three months ended April&nbsp;2, 2006 and
April&nbsp;3, 2005, respectively, which are ultimately reflected as a component of the Company&#146;s cost of
product revenues. At April&nbsp;2, 2006 and January&nbsp;1, 2006, the Company had amounts payable to
Flextronics and its affiliates of approximately $5.9&nbsp;million and $5.4&nbsp;million, respectively, for
these services.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>U3, LLC. </I>The Company and M-Systems entered into an agreement to form U3, LLC, to develop and
market a next generation platform for universal serial bus flash drives. The Company has
consolidated the statement of financial position and the results of operations of U3 for the
quarter ended April&nbsp;2, 2006. The Company&#146;s total investment in U3 as of April&nbsp;2, 2006 was $4.8
million.
</DIV>

<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">19
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>11. Business Acquisition</B>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Matrix Semiconductor. </I>On January&nbsp;13, 2006, the Company completed the acquisition of Matrix
Semiconductor, Inc., or Matrix, a designer and developer of three-dimensional (3-D) integrated
circuits. Matrix<SUP style="font-size: 85%; vertical-align: text-top"><SUP style="font-size: 85%; vertical-align: text-top">&#174;</SUP></SUP> 3-D Memory is used for one-time programmable storage applications
that will complement the Company&#146;s existing flash storage memory products. The Company acquired
100% of the outstanding shares of Matrix for a total purchase price of $296.4&nbsp;million, consisting
of $20.0&nbsp;million in cash, 3,722,591 shares of common stock valued at $242.3&nbsp;million, assumed equity
instruments to issue 567,704 shares of common stock valued at $33.2&nbsp;million and transaction
expenses of $0.9&nbsp;million primarily for accounting and legal fees. The assumed stock options were
valued using the Black-Scholes-Merton valuation model with the following assumptions: stock price
of $65.09; a weighted average volatility rate of 52.8%; a risk-free interest rate of 4.3%; a
dividend yield of zero and a weighted average expected remaining term of 1.4&nbsp;years. The fair value
of unvested assumed stock options, which was valued at the consummation date, will be recognized as
compensation expenses, net of forfeitures, over the remaining vesting period.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The preliminary allocation of Matrix purchase price to the tangible and identifiable
intangible assets acquired and liabilities assumed is summarized below (in thousands). The
preliminary allocation was based on management&#146;s estimates of fair value, which included a
third-party appraisal. The allocation of the purchase price may be subject to change based on
final estimates of fair value, primarily related to deferred taxes.

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The core and developed product technology as a result of the acquisition of Matrix are being
amortized over an estimated useful life of seven years, and the customer relationships are being
amortized over an estimated useful life of three years. No residual value has been estimated for
the intangible assets. In accordance with SFAS 142, the Company will not amortize the goodwill,
but will evaluate it at least annually for impairment.

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">

<DIV align="center" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 18pt"><B>NOTES TO CONDENSED CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS (Cont&#146;d)</B>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Acquisition-Related Restructuring</I>. During the first quarter of fiscal 2006, the Company
established its plans to integrate the Matrix operations primarily by exiting duplicative
facilities and recorded $17.5&nbsp;million for acquisition-related restructuring activities, of which
$17.4&nbsp;million relates to excess lease obligations. The lease obligations extend through the end of
the lease term in 2016. These acquisition-related restructuring liabilities were included in the
purchase price allocation of the cost to acquire Matrix.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>In-process Technology. </I>As part of the Matrix purchase agreement, a certain amount of the
purchase price was allocated to acquired in-process technology which was determined through
established valuation techniques in the high-technology computer industry and written-off in the
first quarter of fiscal 2006 because technological feasibility had not been established and no
alternative future uses existed. The value was determined by estimating the net cash flows and
discounting forecasted net cash flows to their present values. The Company wrote-off the acquired
in-process technology of $39.6&nbsp;million in the first quarter of fiscal 2006. At the time of the
acquisition, it was estimated that these in-process technologies efforts would be completed over
the next one to three years at an estimated total cost of $32.0&nbsp;million.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The net cash flows from the identified projects were based on estimates of revenues, costs of
revenues, research and development expenses, including costs to complete the projects, selling,
marketing and administrative expenses, and income taxes from the projects. The Company believes
the assumptions used in the valuations were reasonable at the time of the acquisition. The
estimated net revenues and gross margins were based on management&#146;s projections of the projects and
were in line with industry averages. Estimated total net revenues from the projects were expected
to grow through fiscal 2009 and decline thereafter as other new products are expected to become
available. Estimated operating expenses included research and development expenses and selling,
marketing and administrative expenses based upon historical and expected direct expense level and
general industry metrics. Estimated research and development expenses included costs to bring the
projects to technological feasibility and costs associated with ongoing maintenance after a product
is released. These activities range from 0% to 5% of net revenues for the in-process technologies.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The effective tax rate used in the analysis of the in-process technologies reflects a
historical industry-specific average for the United States Federal income tax rates. Discount
rates (the rates utilized to discount the net cash flows to their present values) ranging from
12.5% to 15.5% were used in computing the present value of net cash flows for the projects. The
percentage of completion was determined using costs incurred by Matrix prior to the acquisition
date compared to the estimated remaining research and development to be completed to bring the
projects to technological feasibility.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Pro Forma Results. </I>The following unaudited pro forma financial information for the three
months ended April&nbsp;2, 2006 and April&nbsp;3, 2005, presents the combined results of the Company and
Matrix, as if the acquisition had occurred at the beginning of the periods presented. Certain
adjustments have been made to the combined results of operations, including amortization of
acquired other intangible assets; however, charges for acquired in-process technology were excluded
as these items were non-recurring. The pro forma financial results for the three months ended
April&nbsp;2, 2006 and April&nbsp;3, 2005 were as follows:
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>12. Income Taxes</B>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Company recorded tax provisions of $41.3&nbsp;million and $43.8&nbsp;million for the three months
ended April&nbsp;2, 2006 and April&nbsp;3, 2005, or effective tax rates of 54% and 37%, respectively. The
Company&#146;s effective tax rate for the first quarter of fiscal 2006 differed from the statutory
federal rate of 35% primarily due to the impact of non-deductible in-process technology, state
taxes, non-deductible stock option compensation expense recorded under FAS 123(R) and the tax
impact of non-U.S. operations.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The tax benefits associated with stock option activity in the first quarter of fiscal 2006 and
fiscal 2005 reduced taxes payable by $41.9&nbsp;million and $5.4&nbsp;million, respectively. Such benefits
are credited to capital in excess of par value when realized.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>13. Litigation</B>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;From time-to-time, it has been and may continue to be necessary to initiate or defend
litigation against third parties. These and other parties could bring
suit against the Company. In each case listed below where the Company
is the defendant, the Company intends to vigorously defend the action.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On October&nbsp;31, 2001, the Company filed a complaint for patent infringement in the United
States District Court for the Northern District of California against Memorex Products, Inc.,
Pretec Electronics Corporation, Ritek Corporation, and Power Quotient International Co., Ltd. In
the suit, captioned SanDisk Corp. v. Memorex Products, Inc., et al., Civil Case No.&nbsp;CV 01 4063 VRW,
the Company seeks damages and injunctions against these companies from making, selling, importing
or using flash memory cards that infringe its U.S. Patent No.&nbsp;5,602,987. The court granted summary
judgment of non-infringement in favor of defendants Ritek, Pretec and Memorex and entered judgment
on May&nbsp;17, 2004. On June&nbsp;2, 2004, the Company filed a notice of appeal of the summary judgment
rulings to the United States Court of Appeals for the Federal Circuit. On July&nbsp;8, 2005, the
Federal Circuit held in favor of SanDisk, vacating the judgment of non-infringement and remanding
the case back to district court.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On or about June&nbsp;9, 2003, the Company received written notice from Infineon Technologies AG,
or Infineon, that it believes the Company has infringed its U.S. Patent No.&nbsp;5,726,601 (the &#145;601
patent). On June&nbsp;24, 2003, the Company filed a complaint against Infineon for a declaratory
judgment of patent non-infringement and invalidity regarding the &#145;601 patent in the United States
District Court for the Northern District of California, captioned SanDisk Corporation v. Infineon
Technologies AG, a German corporation, et al., Civil Case No.&nbsp;C 03 02931 BZ. On October&nbsp;6, 2003,
Infineon filed an answer and counterclaim: (a)&nbsp;denying that the Company is entitled to the
declaration sought by the Company&#146;s complaint; (b)&nbsp;requesting that the Company be adjudged to have
infringed, actively induced and/or contributed to the infringement of the &#145;601 patent and an
additional patent, U.S. Patent No.&nbsp;4,841,222 (the &#145;222 patent). On August&nbsp;12, 2004, Infineon filed
an amended counterclaim for patent infringement alleging that the Company infringe U.S. Patent Nos.
6,026,002 (the &#145;002 patent); 5,041,894 (the &#145;894 patent); and 6,226,219 (the &#145;219 patent), and
omitting the &#145;601 and &#145;222 patents. On August&nbsp;18, 2004, the Company filed an amended complaint
against Infineon for a declaratory judgment of patent non-infringement and invalidity regarding the
&#145;002, &#145;894, and &#145;219 patents. On February&nbsp;9, 2006, the Company filed a second amended complaint to
include claims for declaratory judgment that the &#145;002, &#145;894 and &#145;219 patents are unenforceable.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On October&nbsp;2, 2003, a purported shareholder class action lawsuit was filed on behalf of United
States holders of ordinary shares of Tower as of the close of business on April&nbsp;1, 2002 in the
United States District Court for the Southern District of New York. The suit, captioned Philippe
de Vries, Julia Frances Dunbar De Vries Trust, et al., v. Tower Semiconductor Ltd., et al., Civil
Case No.&nbsp;03 CV 4999, was filed against Tower and a number of its shareholders and directors,
including the Company and Dr.&nbsp;Harari, who is a Tower board member, and asserts claims arising under
Sections 14(a) and 20(a) of the Securities Exchange Act of 1934, as amended, and Rule&nbsp;14a 9
promulgated there under. The lawsuit alleges that Tower and certain of its directors made false
and misleading statements in a proxy solicitation to Tower shareholders regarding a proposed
amendment to a contract between Tower and certain of its shareholders, including us. The
plaintiffs are seeking unspecified damages and attorneys&#146; and experts&#146; fees and expenses. On
August&nbsp;19, 2004, the court granted our and the other defendants&#146; motion to dismiss the complaint in
its entirety with prejudice. On September&nbsp;29, 2004, plaintiffs appealed the dismissal to the
United States Court of Appeals for the Second Circuit.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On February&nbsp;20, 2004, the Company and a number of other manufacturers of flash memory products
were sued in the Superior Court of the State of California for the City and County of San Francisco
in a purported consumer class action captioned Willem Vroegh et al. v. Dane Electric Corp. USA, et
al., Civil Case No.&nbsp;GCG 04 428953, alleging false advertising, unfair business practices, breach of
contract, fraud, deceit, misrepresentation and violation of the California Consumers Legal Remedy
Act. The lawsuit purports to be on behalf of a class of purchasers of flash memory products and
claims that the defendants overstated the size of the memory storage capabilities of such products.
The lawsuit seeks restitution, injunction and damages in an unspecified amount. The parties have
reached a settlement of the case, which is pending final court approval.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On October&nbsp;15, 2004, the Company filed a complaint for patent infringement and declaratory
judgment of non-infringement and patent invalidity against STMicroelectronics N.V. and
STMicroelectronics, Inc. in the United States District Court for the Northern District of
California, captioned SanDisk Corporation v. STMicroelectronics, Inc., et al., Civil Case No.&nbsp;C 04
04379JF. The complaint alleges that STMicro&#146;s products infringe one of the Company&#146;s U.S. patents
and seeks damages and an injunction. The complaint further seeks a declaratory judgment that the
Company does not infringe several of STMicro&#146;s U.S. patents. By
order dated January&nbsp;4, 2005, the court stayed the Company&#146;s claim that STMicro infringes the
Company&#146;s patent pending an outcome in the ITC investigation initiated on November&nbsp;15, 2004
(discussed below). On January&nbsp;20, 2005, the court issued an order granting STMicro&#146;s motion to
dismiss the declaratory judgment causes of action. The Company has appealed this decision to the
U.S. Court of Appeals for the Federal Circuit. The remainder of the case, including the Company&#146;s
infringement claim against STMicro, is stayed pending the outcome of the appeal.
</DIV>

<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">22
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On February&nbsp;4, 2005, STMicro filed two complaints for patent infringement against the Company
in the United States District Court for the Eastern District of Texas, captioned
STMicroelectronics, Inc. v. SanDisk Corporation, Civil Case No.&nbsp;4 05CV44, and STMicroelectronics,
Inc. v. SanDisk Corporation, Civil Case No.&nbsp;4 05CV45, respectively. The complaints seek damages
and injunctions against unspecified SanDisk products. On April&nbsp;22, 2005, the Company filed
counterclaims on two patents against STMicroelectronics N.V. and STMicroelectronics, Inc. in the
Civil Case 4-05CV45 proceeding. The counterclaims seek damages and injunctive relief against
STMicroelectronics N.V. and STMicroelectronics, Inc. flash memory products.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On October&nbsp;15, 2004, the Company filed a complaint under Section&nbsp;337 of the Tariff Act of 1930
(as amended) titled, &#147;In the matter of certain NAND flash memory circuits and products containing
same&#148; in the United States International Trade Commission, naming STMicroelectronics N.V. and
STMicroelectronics, Inc. (&#147;STMicro&#148;) as respondents. In the complaint, the Company alleges that
STMicro&#146;s NAND flash memory infringes U.S. Patent No.&nbsp;5,172,338 (the &#145;338 patent), and seek an
order excluding their products from importation into the United States. In the complaint, the
Company alleges that STMicro&#146;s NAND flash memory infringes the &#145;338 patent and seeks an order
excluding their products from importation into the United States. On November&nbsp;15, 2004, the ITC
instituted an investigation pursuant to 19 U.S.C. Section&nbsp;1337 against STMicro in response to the
Company&#146;s complaint. A hearing was held from August 1-8, 2005. On October&nbsp;19, 2005, the
Administrative Law Judge issued an initial determination confirming the validity and enforceability
of the Company&#146;s United States Patent 5,172,338 (&#145;338 patent) by rejecting STMicro&#146;s claims that
the patent was invalidated by prior art. The initial determination, however, found that STMicro&#146;s
NAND flash memory chips did not infringe three claims of the &#145;338 patent. On October&nbsp;31, 2005, the
Company filed a petition with the International Trade Commission to review and reverse the finding
of non-infringement. Also, on October&nbsp;31, 2005, STMicro filed a petition for review with the
International Trade Commission to review and reverse the finding that the patent was valid and
enforceable. On December&nbsp;6, 2005, the ITC issued its decision. The ITC declined to review the
finding of non-infringement, and, after reviewing the finding of validity, declined to take any
position on the issue of validity. The Company is appealing the ITC&#146;s decision to the U.S. Court
of Appeals for the Federal Circuit.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On October&nbsp;14, 2005, STMicroelectronics, Inc. filed a complaint against the Company and the
Company&#146;s CEO Eli Harari, in the Superior Court of the State of California for the County of
Alameda, captioned STMicroelectronics, Inc. v. Harari, Case No.&nbsp;HG 05237216. The complaint alleges
that STMicroelectronics, Inc., as the successor to Wafer Scale Integration, Inc.&#146;s (&#147;WSI&#148;) legal
rights, has an ownership interest in several SanDisk patents that issued from applications filed by
Dr.&nbsp;Harari, a former WSI employee. The complaint seeks the
assignment or co-ownership of certain inventions and
patents conceived of by Harari, including some of the patents
asserted by the Company in its litigations against STMicro, as well as damages in an unspecified amount. On November&nbsp;15, 2005,
Harari and the Company removed the case to the U.S. District Court for the Northern District of
California, where it was assigned case number C05-04691. On November&nbsp;23, 2005, Harari and the
Company filed counterclaims, asserting our (i.e., SanDisk&#146;s) ownership of the patents and
applications raised in the complaint. On December&nbsp;13, 2005, STMicroelectronics, Inc. filed a
motion to remand the case back to the Superior Court of Alameda County. STMicro&#146;s remand motion
was denied by the Court in March&nbsp;2006. On April&nbsp;24, 2006, Dr.&nbsp;Harari and the Company filed a
motion for summary judgment on statute of limitations and other grounds that, if granted, would
result in dismissal of all of STMicro&#146;s claims.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On December&nbsp;6, 2005, the Company filed a complaint for patent infringement in the United
States District Court for the Northern District of California against STMicroelectronics, Inc. and
STMicroelectronics, NV (&#147;STMicro&#148;) (Case No.&nbsp;C0505021 JF). In the suit, the Company seeks damages
and injunctions against STMicro from making, selling, importing or using flash memory chips or
products that infringe the Company&#146;s U.S. Patent No.&nbsp;5,991,517. The case is presently stayed,
pending the termination of the ITC investigation instituted February&nbsp;8, 2006, discussed below.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On January&nbsp;11, 2006, the Company filed a complaint for patent infringement in the United
States District Court for the Northern District of California against STMicro (Case No.C06-00194
JF). In the suit, the Company seeks damages and injunctions against STMicro from making, selling,
importing or using flash memory chips or products that infringe the Company&#146;s U.S. Patent No.
6,542,956. The case is presently stayed, pending the termination of the ITC investigation
instituted February&nbsp;8, 2006, discussed below.
</DIV>

<DIV style="font-family: 'Times New Roman',Times,serif">

<DIV align="center" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 18pt"><B>NOTES TO CONDENSED CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS (Cont&#146;d)</B>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On January&nbsp;10, 2006, the Company filed a complaint under Section&nbsp;337 of the Tariff Act of 1930
(as amended) titled, &#147;In the matter of certain NAND flash memory circuits and products containing
same&#148; in the ITC, naming STMicro as respondents. In the complaint, the Company allege that: (i)
STMicro&#146;s NOR flash memory infringes the &#145;338 patent; (ii)&nbsp;STMicro&#146;s NAND flash memory infringes
U.S. Patent No.&nbsp;6,542,956; and (iii)&nbsp;STMicro&#146;s NOR flash memory and NAND flash memory infringe U.S.
Patent No.&nbsp;5,991,517. The complaint seeks an order excluding STMicro&#146;s NOR and NAND flash memory
products from importation into the United States. The ITC instituted an investigation, based on
the Company&#146;s complaint, on February&nbsp;8, 2006. On March&nbsp;31, 2006, STMicro filed a motion for
partial summary determination or termination of the investigation with respect to the &#145;338 patent.
On May&nbsp;1, 2006, the Administrative Law Judge denied STMicro&#146;s motion in an initial determination
that is subject to review by the ITC.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On or about July&nbsp;15, 2005, Societa&#146; Italiana Per Lo Sviluppo Dell&#146;electtronica, S.I.Sv.El.,
S.p.A., (&#147;Sisvel&#148;) filed suit against us and others in the district court of the Netherlands in The
Hague in a case captioned Societa&#146; Italiana Per Lo Sviluppo Dell&#146;electtronica, S.I.Sv.El., S.p.A.
adverse to SanDisk International Sales, Moduslink B.V. and UPS SCS (Nederland) B.V., Case No.
999.131.1804. Sisvel alleges that certain of the Company&#146;s MP3 products infringe three European
patents of which Sisvel claims to be a licensee with the right to bring suit. Sisvel seeks an
injunction and unspecified damages. Sisvel has previously publicly indicated that it will license
these and other patents under reasonable and nondiscriminatory terms, and it has specifically
offered the Company a license under the patents. The Company has submitted pleadings asking the
court to strike Sisvel&#146;s pleadings as legally insufficient and seeking other procedural relief.
The court is still addressing these procedural matters and the Company will not be required to
answer on the substance of Sisvel&#146;s claim until late May&nbsp;2006 at the earliest.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In a related action, on February&nbsp;21, 2006, the Company filed an action in the English High
Court, Chancery Division, Patents Court, in London, against the owners of the patents Sisvel has
asserted against the Company. The case is SanDisk Corporation v. Koninklijke Philips Electronics
N.V. (a Dutch corporation), France T&#233;l&#233;com (a French corporation), T&#233;l&#233;diffusion de France S.A. (a
French corporation), and Institut f&#252;r Rundfunktechnik GmbH (a German corporation), Case No.&nbsp;HC06 C
00615. In this action, the Company seeks a declaration that the patents asserted by Sisvel (as
well as other patents owned by Philips and the other defendants) are invalid because they fail to
properly claim anything new within the meaning of the European Patent Convention and because
certain of them fail to comply with other requirements of the Convention. The defendants in that
case have appeared and announced their intention to defend. The defendants&#146; formal defense will be
due in early May&nbsp;2006. On April&nbsp;24, 2006, the Company filed a motion for summary judgment, asking
the court to hold five of the defendants&#146; UK patents invalid. The hearing on that motion will
likely take place in or after July&nbsp;2006.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In another related action, on March&nbsp;9, 2006, the Company filed an action in the English High
Court, Chancery Division, Patents Court, in London, against Sisvel and the owners of the patents
Sisvel has asserted against us in the Netherlands. The case is SanDisk Corporation v. Koninklijke
Philips Electronics N.V. (a Dutch corporation), France T&#233;l&#233;com (a French corporation),
T&#233;l&#233;diffusion de France S.A. (a French corporation), Institut f&#252;r Rundfunktechnik GmbH (a German
corporation) and Societa&#146; Italiana Per Lo Sviluppo Dell&#146;electtronica, S.I.Sv.El., S.p.A., Case No.
HC06C00835. In this action, the Company seeks a declaration of non-infringement of the patents
asserted by Sisvel in connection with the Company&#146;s MP3 products. The Company also seeks a
declaration that the patents are not &#147;essential&#148; to the technology of MP3 players, as Sisvel
presently contends in the case filed in the Netherlands. The defendants have appeared and
announced their intention to defend. The defendants&#146; formal defense will be due in early May&nbsp;2006.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In another related action, on April&nbsp;13, 2006, Audio MPEG filed a complaint alleging patent
infringement in the District Court for the Eastern District of Virginia. The case is Audio MPEG v.
SanDisk Corporation, Case No.&nbsp;2:06cv209 WDK/JEB. Audio MPEG holds itself out to be the U.S.
subsidiary of Sisvel and purports to have the right to enforce certain patents in the U.S. on
subject matter related to the patents asserted by Sisvel in the Netherlands. Specifically, Audio
MPEG asserts U.S. Patent No.&nbsp;5,214,678 (entitled &#147;Digital transmission system using subband coding
of a digital signal&#148;), U.S. Patent No.&nbsp;5,323,396 (entitled &#147;Digital transmission system,
transmitter and receiver for use in the transmission system&#148;), U.S. Patent No.&nbsp;5,539,829 (entitled
&#147;Subband coded digital transmission system using some composite signals&#148;), and U.S. Patent No.
5,777,992 (entitled &#147;Decoder for decoding and encoded digital signal and a receiver comprising the
decoder&#148;). The complaint seeks damages and injunctive relief. The Company responded promptly,
filing a motion to dismiss on April&nbsp;20, 2006, asking the court to dismiss the complaint on the
grounds that Audio MPEG failed to join the patent holders as co-plaintiffs. That motion could be
ready for decision as soon as May&nbsp;2006.
</DIV>

<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">24
</DIV>

<DIV align="center" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 18pt"><B>NOTES TO CONDENSED CONSOLIDATED FINANCIAL STATEMENTS (Cont&#146;d)</B>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In another related action, on April&nbsp;14, 2006, the Company filed suit in the District Court for
the Northern District of California against Audio MPEG and the owners of the patents Audio MPEG is
asserting the Virginia court. The case is SanDisk Corporation v. Audio MPEG, U.S. Philips Corp.,
France T&#233;l&#233;com, T&#233;l&#233;diffusion de France S.A., and Institut f&#252;r Rundfunktechnik GMBH, Case No.
C06-02655 MEJ. In this case, the Company seeks a declaration from the court that the Company is
not infringing any valid claim of U.S. Patent No.&nbsp;5,214,678 (entitled &#147;Digital transmission system
using subband coding of a digital signal&#148;), U.S. Patent No.&nbsp;5,323,396 (entitled &#147;Digital
transmission system, transmitter and receiver for use in the transmission system&#148;), U.S. Patent No.
5,539,829 (entitled &#147;Subband coded digital transmission system using some composite signals&#148;), and
U.S. Patent No.&nbsp;5,777,992 (entitled &#147;Decoder for decoding and encoded digital signal and a receiver
comprising the decoder&#148;).
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>14. Subsequent Events</B>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On April&nbsp;28, 2006, the Company and Toshiba agreed to accelerate the expansion of Fab 3, which
is expected to bring Fab 3 wafer capacity from the previously planned 70,000 wafers per month to
90,000 wafers per month by April&nbsp;2007. The incremental investment by the Company for 50% of this
higher Fab 3 output is currently estimated at approximately $300&nbsp;million over the next 12&nbsp;months.
The Company&#146;s total investment to bring Fab 3 wafer capacity to 90,000 wafers per month is expected
to be approximately $1.9&nbsp;billion. The Company expects to fund its portion of the investment
through its cash as well as other financing sources.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>Item&nbsp;2. Management&#146;s Discussion and Analysis of Financial Condition and Results of
Operations</B>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;<I>Statements in this report, which are not historical facts, are forward-looking statements
within the meaning of the federal securities laws. These statements may contain words such as
&#147;expects,&#148; &#147;anticipates,&#148; &#147;intends,&#148; &#147;plans,&#148; &#147;believes,&#148; &#147;seeks,&#148; &#147;estimates&#148; or other wording
indicating future results or expectations. Forward-looking statements are subject to significant
risks and uncertainties. Our actual results may differ materially from the results discussed in
these forward-looking statements. Factors that could cause our actual results to differ materially
include, but are not limited to, those discussed under &#147;Risk Factors&#148; in this report and elsewhere
in this report. Our business, financial condition or results of operations could be materially
adversely affected by any of these factors. We undertake no obligation to revise or update any
forward-looking statements to reflect any event or circumstance that arises after the date of this
report, except as required by law. References in this report to &#147;SanDisk</I><SUP style="font-size: 85%; vertical-align: text-top"><I><SUP style="font-size: 85%; vertical-align: text-top">&#174;</SUP></I></SUP><I>,&#148; &#147;we,&#148;
&#147;our,&#148; and &#147;us&#148; collectively refer to SanDisk Corporation, a Delaware corporation, and its
subsidiaries.</I>
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 12pt"><B>Overview</B>
</DIV>


<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;We
are the worldwide leader in flash storage card products. We design, develop and market
flash storage devices used in a wide variety of consumer electronics products. Flash storage
allows data to be stored in a compact format that retains the data for an extended period of time
after the power has been turned off. Our flash storage card products enable mass-market adoption
of digital cameras, feature phones, MP3 players and other digital consumer devices. Our products
include flash cards, Universal Serial Bus, or USB, flash drives and digital audio players.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;As a supplier to this industry, our results are primarily driven by worldwide demand for flash
storage devices, which in turn depends on end-user demand for electronic products. We believe the
market for flash storage is price elastic. We expect that as we reduce the price of our flash
devices, consumers will demand an increasing number of megabytes of memory. In order to profitably
capitalize on price elasticity in the market for flash storage products, we must reduce our cost
per megabyte at a rate similar to the change in selling price per megabyte to the consumer. We
achieve these cost reductions through technology improvements primarily focused on increasing the
amount of memory stored in a given area of silicon.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In January&nbsp;2006, we acquired Matrix Semiconductor, Inc., or Matrix, a designer and developer
of three-dimensional (3-D) integrated circuits. Matrix<SUP style="font-size: 85%; vertical-align: text-top"><SUP style="font-size: 85%; vertical-align: text-top">&#174;</SUP></SUP> 3-D Memory is used for one-time
programmable storage applications that will complement our existing flash storage memory products.
Matrix 3-D Memory is used for storage applications that do not require rewriteable memory and where
low cost is the paramount consideration, such as video games, music and other content, or for
archiving. The acquisition of Matrix resulted in a $39.6&nbsp;million write-off of in-process acquired
technology during the first quarter of fiscal 2006.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In April&nbsp;2006, we and Toshiba Corporation, or Toshiba, entered into a non-binding memorandum
of understanding to build Fab 4, a proposed new advanced 300-millimeter wafer fabrication facility at Toshiba&#146;s
Yokkaichi, Japan operations to meet the anticipated fast growing demand for NAND flash memory in
2008 and beyond. We and Toshiba plan to start construction of the new facility in August&nbsp;2006,
with initial production operations scheduled to begin in the fourth quarter of 2007. Toshiba will
fund construction of the building, while both we and Toshiba will provide funds for the
manufacturing equipment. When full production is achieved, Fab 4 is anticipated to be similar in
capacity to the 300-millimeter Fab 3 wafer facility now in operation at Yokkaichi.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Beginning in the first quarter of fiscal 2006, we adopted the fair value recognition
provisions of Statement of Financial Accounting Standards No.&nbsp;123(R), or FAS 123(R), <I>Share Based
Payments</I>, using the modified-prospective transition method. Under that transition method,
compensation cost recognized in the first quarter of fiscal 2006 include the following: (a)
compensation cost related to any share-based awards granted through, but not yet vested as of
January&nbsp;1, 2006, and (b)&nbsp;compensation cost for any share-based awards granted on or subsequent to
January&nbsp;2, 2006, based on the grant-date fair value estimated in accordance with the provisions of
SFAS 123(R). As a result of adopting SFAS 123(R), we recognized share-based employee compensation
expense of $18.8&nbsp;million during the first quarter of fiscal 2006, which affected our reported
research and development, selling and marketing and general and administrative expenses. In
addition, we capitalized to inventory $2.5&nbsp;million of compensation cost for stock-based awards that
were issued to manufacturing personnel. We calculated this expense based on the fair values of the
share-based compensation awards as estimated using the Black-Scholes-Merton closed-form option
valuation model. As of April&nbsp;2, 2006, total unrecognized compensation expense related to unvested
share-based compensation arrangements already granted under our various plans was $231.0&nbsp;million,
which we expect will be recognized over a weighted-average period of 1.4&nbsp;years.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The increase in our product revenues for the first quarter of fiscal 2006 compared to the
first quarter of fiscal 2005 was comprised of a 164% increase in the number of megabytes sold,
partially offset by a 49% reduction in our average selling price per megabyte. Our year over year
revenue growth was primarily due to increased sales of cards for handsets, cards for gaming
devices, and digital audio players. Our first quarter 2006 OEM business represented 31% of our
product revenues, up from 21% in the first quarter of fiscal 2005 due primarily to increased sales
of cards to handset manufacturers. We expect to continue to reduce our price per megabyte as
technology advances allow us to further reduce our cost per megabyte.
</DIV>

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Our top ten customers represented approximately 49% and 58% of our total revenues in the first
quarters of fiscal 2006 and fiscal 2005, respectively. No customer exceeded 10% of total revenues
in either of these quarters except Samsung Electronics Co. Ltd., which was 14% in the first quarter
of fiscal 2006, including sales of our products and royalty revenues.
</DIV>

<P align="center" style="font-size: 10pt">27
</DIV>

increase in revenue from other foreign countries primarily due to the location of our customers
that are purchasing cards for handsets and an increase in revenue from EMEA due primarily to growth
in our retail sales in that region.

operations after a brief power failure in the first quarter of fiscal 2006. Stock compensation
expense of $2.5&nbsp;million was capitalized in inventory in the first fiscal quarter of 2006 and will
be recognized as cost of sales as product is sold.

<DIV align="left" style="font-size: 10pt; margin-top: 6pt">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;As part of the Matrix purchase agreement, a certain amount of the purchase price was allocated
to acquired in-process technology which was determined through established valuation techniques in
the high-technology computer industry and written-off in the first quarter of fiscal 2006 because
technological feasibility had not been established and no alternative future uses existed. The
value was determined by estimating the net cash flows and discounting forecasted net cash flows to
their present values. At the time of the acquisition, it was estimated that these in-process
technologies efforts would be completed over the next one to three years at an estimated total cost
of $32.0&nbsp;million. See Note 11, &#147;Business Acquisition.&#148;
